            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, lithium-ion batteries were attracting more interest for use in automotive applications.  Lithium resources are confirmed to be unevenly distributed in South America, and the cost of the lithium raw materials has roughly doubled from the first practical application in 1991 to the present and is increasing due to global demand for lithium-ion accumulators.  Since the electrochem. equiv. and std. potential of sodium are the most advantageous after lithium, sodium based energy storage is of great interest to realize lithium-free high energy and high voltage batteries.  However, to the best of authors knowledge, there were no successful reports on electrochem. sodium insertion materials for battery applications; the major challenge is the neg. electrode and its passivation.  In this study, high capacity and excellent reversibility are achieved of sodium-insertion performance of hard-carbon and layered NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 electrodes in propylene carbonate electrolyte solns.  The structural change and passivation for hard-carbon are investigated to study the reversible sodium insertion.  The 3-V secondary Na-ion battery possessing environmental and cost friendliness, Na+-shuttlecock hard-carbon/NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 cell, demonstrates steady cycling performance as next generation secondary batteries and an alternative to Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrp5J70QNujrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljpLtltxnqk1A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhtVWjurfM&amp;md5=be5cae72214fa773ada0e3fcca7b49d1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2013.01.064"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S. X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Reduced Graphene Oxide with Superior Cycling Stability and Rate Capability for Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>57</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">202</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">208</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.carbon.2013.01.064</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D57%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D202-208%26journal%3DCarbon%26author%3DY.%2BX.%2BWang%26author%3DS.%2BL.%2BChou%26author%3DH.%2BK.%2BLiu%26author%3DS.%2BX.%2BDou%26title%3DReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BCycling%2BStability%2Band%2BRate%2BCapability%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.carbon.2013.01.064&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b12204&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.carbon.2013.01.064&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reduced graphene oxide with superior cycling stability and rate capability for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yun-Xiao; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">57</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">202-208</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries are promising elec. energy storage systems for sustainable energy storage applications due to the abundance of Na and their low cost.  The electrochem. properties of Na ion storage in reduced graphene oxide (RGO) were studied in an electrolyte consisting of 1 M NaClO4 in propylene carbonate (PC).  The RGO anode allowed significant Na ion insertion, leading to higher capacity at high c.d. compared to the previously reported results for C materials.  This is due to the fact that RGO possesses higher elec. cond. and is a more active host, with large interlayer distances and a disordered structure, enabling it to store more Na ions.  RGO anode exhibits high capacity combined with long-term cycling stability at high current densities, leading to reversible capacity ≤174.3 mA-h g-1 at 0.2 C (40 mA g-1), and even 93.3 mA-h g-1 at 1 C (200 mA g-1) after 250 cycles.  Also, RGO could yield a high capacity of 141 mA-h g-1 at 0.2 C (40 mA g-1) over 1000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr39AqQSVabh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljpLtltxnqk1A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXjtVensLc%253D&amp;md5=704c607778e4fad1ece37d5d579584eb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1021/ja310347x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Darwiche, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marino, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sougrati, M.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Marino, Cyril; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Fraisse, Bernard; Stievano, Lorenzo; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfZ6rvnJyfxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liz2a8kYVkyFg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhslCgsbnE&amp;md5=75362e7708fe6434655290ce0aa7cac0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201502000"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, Y.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-Protected 3D Sb-based Anodes Fabricated via Electrostatic Assembly and Confinement Replacement for Enhanced Lithium and Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Yuan-Li; Wu, Chao; Kopold, Peter; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Alloy anodes have shown great potential for next-generation lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, these applications are still limited by inherent huge vol. changes and sluggish kinetics.  To overcome such limitations, graphene-protected 3D Sb-based anodes grown on conductive substrate are designed and fabricated by a facile electrostatic-assembling and subsequent confinement replacement strategy.  As binder-free anodes for LIBs, the obtained electrode exhibits reversible capacities of 442 mAh/g at 100 mA/g and 295 mAh/g at 1000 mA/g, and a capacity retention of above 90% (based on the 10th cycle) after 200 cycles at 500 mA/g.  As for sodium storage properties, the reversible capacities of 517 mAh/g at 50 mA/g and 315 mAh/g at 1000 mA/g, the capacity retention of 305 mAh/g after 100 cycles at 300 mA/g are obtained, resp.  Furthermore, the 3D architecture retains good structural integrity after cycling, confirming that the introduction of high-stretchy and robust graphene layers can effectively buffer alloying anodes, and simultaneously provide sustainable contact and protection of the active materials.  Such findings show its great potential as superior binder-free anodes for LIBs and SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGodL23xy3aRnLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liz2a8kYVkyFg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1elurfF&amp;md5=ff71a1c541fff6a590497c868c41e134</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201209689"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Template-Free Electrochemical Synthesis of Sn Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode Materials for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nam, Do-Hwan; Kim, Tae-Hee; Hong, Kyung-Sik; Kwon, Hyuk-Sang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sn nanofibers with a high aspect ratio are successfully synthesized using a simple electrodeposition process from an aq. soln. without the use of templates.  The synthesis approach involves the rapid electrochem. deposition of Sn accompanied by the strong adsorption of Triton X-100, which can function as a growth modifier for the Sn crystallites.  Triton X-100 is adsorbed on the {200} crystallog. planes of Sn in an elongated configuration and suppressed the preferential growth of Sn along the [100] direction.  Consequently, the Sn electrodeposits are forced to grow anisotropically in a direction normal to the (112) or (‾112) plane, forming one-dimensional nanofibers.  As electrode materials for the Na-ion batteries, the Sn nanofibers exhibit a high reversible capacity and an excellent cycle performance; the charge capacity is maintained at 776.26 mA-h/g after 100 cycles, which corresponds to a retention of 95.09% of the initial charge capacity.  The superior electrochem. performance of the Sn nanofibers is mainly attributed to the high mech. stability of the nanofibers, which originate from highly anisotropic expansion during sodiation and the pore vols. existing between the nanofibers.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpMet3lkd_Y6bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liz2a8kYVkyFg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVegu7rN&amp;md5=76f47655b744f6cccb1ae0ba7a7760d4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200346"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical performance of porous carbon/tin composite anodes for sodium-ion and lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Yunhua; Zhu, Yujie; Liu, Yihang; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. performance of mesoporous carbon (C)/tin (Sn) anodes in Na-ion and Li-ion batteries is systematically investigated.  The mesoporous C/Sn anodes in a Na-ion battery shows similar cycling stability but lower capacity and poorer rate capability than that in a Li-ion battery.  The desodiation potentials of Sn anodes are approx. 0.21 V lower than delithiation potentials.  The low capacity and poor rate capability of C/Sn anode in Na-ion batteries is mainly due to the large Na-ion size, resulting in slow Na-ion diffusion and large vol. change of porous C/Sn composite anode during alloy/dealloy reactions.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin nanoparticles encapsulated in graphene backboned carbonaceous foams as high-performance anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Bin; Qiu, Tengfei; Ye, Delai; Wang, Lianzhou; Zhi, Linjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new type of hierarchical tin@carbon composite composed of graphene carbonaceous matrix and well-confined tin nanoparticles with a typical size of ∼15 nm (denoted as F-G/Sn@C) is developed and investigated as anode material for Li-ion and Na-ion storage.  The two dimensional graphene backboned matrix not only acts as a confinement layer preventing the tin nanoparticles from aggregating during the material prepn., but also functions as a phys. barrier to buffer the vol. change effect during charge/discharge processes.  As a consequence, the composite demonstrates excellent rate performance and cycling stability for both Li-ion and Na-ion storage.  In particular, the F-G/Sn@C anode exhibits an impressive reversible capacity of 506 mAh g-1 even after 500 cycles and a high-rate capacity of 270 mAh g-1 even at 3200 mA g-1 for Li-ion storage.  Moreover, a reversible Na-ion storage capacity of 413 mAh g-1 with negligible fading is also achieved.  The remarkable electrochem. performance, together with the facile synthetic approach for large scale prodn., enables such material as a highly attractive tin-based anode for next generation rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXsgmx8FWKsLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhHfH0yT-4hIw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xjt1Wlsbs%253D&amp;md5=de71d232cab95a81d764c84864d4920a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.08.044"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Patra, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High dispersion of 1-nm SnO2 particles between graphene nanosheets constructed using supercritical CO2 fluid for sodium-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Patra, Jagabandhu; Chen, Hung-Ching; Yang, Cheng-Hsien; Hsieh, Chien-Te; Su, Ching-Yuan; Chang, Jeng-Kuei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Supercrit.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A highly stable (SnOx-Sn)@few layered graphene composite anode of sodium-ion batteries synthesized by oxygen plasma assisted milling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Deliang; Liu, Jiangwen; Li, Xiang; Hu, Renzong; Zeng, Meiqing; Yang, Lichun; Zhu, Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The (SnOx-Sn)@few layered graphene ((SnOx-Sn)@FLG) composite has been synthesized by O plasma-assisted milling.  Owing to the synergistic effect of rapid plasma heating and ball mill grinding, SnOx (1≤ x ≤2) nanoparticles generated from the reaction of Sn with O are tightly wrapped by FLG nanosheets which are simultaneously exfoliated from expanded graphite, forming secondary micro granules.  Inside the granules, the small size of the SnOx nanoparticles enables the fast kinetics for Na+ transfer.  The in-situ formed FLG and residual Sn nanoparticles improve the elec. cond. of the composite, meanwhile alleviate the aggregation of SnOx nanoparticles and relieve the vol. change during the cycling, which is beneficial for the cyclic stability for the Na+ storage.  As an anode material for Na-ion batteries, the (SnOx-Sn)@FLG composite exhibits a high reversible capacity of 448 mAh/g at a c.d. of 100 mA/g in the 1st cycle, with 82.6% capacity retention after 250 cycles.  Even when the c.d. increases to 1000 mA/g, this composite retains 316.5 mAh/g after 250 cycles.  With superior Na+ storage stability, the (SnOx-Sn)@FLG composite can be a promising anode material for high performance sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpu3VJ7Z_IUi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhHfH0yT-4hIw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkslyjtrY%253D&amp;md5=411e9333c9fa824c27eb67deca3362e6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1039/c3cc40448j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been considered as promising alternatives to Li-ion batteries due to the natural abundance of sodium resources.  Searching for high-performance anode materials currently becomes a hot topic and also a great challenge for developing Na-ion batteries.  In this work, a novel hybrid anode is synthesized consisting of ultrafine, few-layered SnS2 anchored on few-layered reduced graphene oxide (rGO) by a facile solvothermal route.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">First Introduction of NiSe2 to Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries: A Hybrid of Graphene-Wrapped NiSe2/C Porous Nanofiber</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cho, Jung Sang; Lee, Seung Yeon; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific Reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">23338</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The first-ever study of nickel selenide materials as efficient anode materials for Na-ion rechargeable batteries is conducted using the electrospinning process.  NiSe2-reduced graphene oxide (rGO)-C composite nanofibers are successfully prepd. via electrospinning and a subsequent selenization process.  The electrospun nanofibers giving rise to these porous-structured composite nanofibers with optimum amt. of amorphous C are obtained from the polystyrene to polyacrylonitrile ratio of 1/4.  These composite nanofibers also consist of uniformly distributed single-cryst. NiSe2 nanocrystals that have a mean size of 27 nm.  In contrast, the densely structured bare NiSe2 nanofibers formed via selenization of the pure NiO nanofibers consist of large crystallites.  The initial discharge capacities of the NiSe2-rGO-C composite and bare NiSe2 nanofibers at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1 are 717 and 755 mA h g-1, resp.  However, the resp. 100th-cycle discharge capacities of the former and latter are 468 and 35 mA h g-1.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy measurements reveal the structural stability of the composite nanofibers during repeated Na-ion insertion and extn. processes.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">SnSe/carbon nanocomposite synthesized by high energy ball milling as an anode material for sodium-ion and lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Zhian; Zhao, Xingxing; Li, Jie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A homogeneous nanocomposite of SnSe and C black, denoted as SnSe/C nanocomposite, was fabricated by high energy ball milling and employed as a high performance anode material for both Na-ion batteries and Li-ion batteries.  The x-ray diffraction patterns, SEM and TEM observations confirmed that SnSe in SnSe/C nanocomposite was homogeneously distributed within C black.  The nanocomposite anode exhibited enhanced electrochem. performances including a high capacity, long cycling behavior and good rate performance in both Na-ion batteries (SIBs) and Li-ion batteries (LIBs).                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superior Na-ion storage properties of high aspect ratio SnSe nanoplates prepared by a spray pyrolysis process</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Gi Dae; Lee, Jong-Heun; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnSe nanoplates with thin and uniform morphol. are prepd. by one-pot spray pyrolysis, and are examd. as anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  During the spray pyrolysis process, metallic Se and Sn are prepd. from SeO2 and SnO2, resp., under a reducing atm.  Metallic Sn and metalloid Se, with m.ps. of 232 and 221 °C, resp., form a melted Sn-Se mixt., which reacts exothermally to form SnSe nanocrystals.  Several of these nanocrystals are grown simultaneously forming a micron-sized powder.  Complete elimination of the excess amt. of metalloid Se, by forming H2Se gas, results in aggregation-free SnSe nanoplates.  The aspect ratio of these nanoplates is as high as 11.3.  The discharge capacities for the SnSe nanoplates, prepd. from spray solns. contg. 100, 400, and 800% of the stoichiometric SeO2 content needed to form SnSe, are 407, 558, and 211 mA h g-1, resp., after 50 cycles at a const. c.d. of 0.3 A g-1; their capacity retentions calcd. from the second cycle onwards are 77, 100, and 60%, resp.  The phase pure SnSe nanoplates with a high aspect ratio show good cycling and rate performances for Na-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqPRAiSkrJFcLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljuJm9QjYJLGQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XnslGksbY%253D&amp;md5=bd2dfa41fa2480c4df38fc5076dee26b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b01829"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, D.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin selenides with layered crystal structures, SnSe and SnSe2, were synthesized by a solid-state method and electrochem. tested for use as Li-ion battery anodes.  The phase change mechanisms of these compds. were thoroughly evaluated by ex situ X-ray diffraction and Se K-edge extended X-ray absorption fine structure techniques.  SnSe showed better electrochem. reversibility of Li insertion/extn. than SnSe2, which was attributed to remarkable conversion/recombination reactions of the former compd. during lithiation/delithiation.  Addnl., the electrochem. performance of SnSe was further enhanced by prepg. carbon-modified nanocomposites using two different methods, i.e., heat treatment (HT) for producing a carbon coating using polyvinyl chloride as a precursor and high-energy ball milling (BM) using carbon black powder.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Investigation of electrochemical performance on carbon supported tin-selenium bimetallic anodes in lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yoon, Young Hoon; Kim, Doo Soo; Kim, Min Jung; Park, Min Sang; Lee, Young-Chul; Kim, Kwang Ho; Kim, Il Tae; Hur, Jaehyun; Lee, Seung Geol</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">266</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bimetallic compd., composed of two different metal elements, has emerged as an important class of electrode system.  Amorphous C materials are widely used in anodes to reduce the internal resistance of electrodes.  Therefore, SnSe bimetallic compd. uniformly dispersed in acetylene black as a C-support was fabricated for Li ion batteries by high energy mech. milling (HEMM) process under Ar atm.  The SnSe-C composite retains a reversible capacity of 564 mAh g-1 with a coulombic efficiency of 99.8%, at a current rate of 100 mA g-1 after 50 cycles.  In the high rate capability test, the SnSe-C composite exhibits the charge capacity of 530 mAh g-1 at 5000 mA g-1 charge rate.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) results indicate that SnSe-C composite shows small increase of surface resistance than that of plain SnSe composite.  The enhanced cycle stability of SnSe-C composite can be attributed to the amorphous C additive that offers high elec. cond. as well as a buffer matrix that prevents the vol. change during cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo2zB71bW1INLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljuJm9QjYJLGQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXisFCksro%253D&amp;md5=7a55efbbe4806cad66378b5bb0210273</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.06.065"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gurung, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Naderi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vaagensmith, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Varnekar, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Selenide - Multi-Walled Carbon Nanotubes Hybrid Anodes for High Performance Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gurung, Ashim; Naderi, Roya; Vaagensmith, Bjorn; Varnekar, Geetha; Zhou, Zhengping; Elbohy, Hytham; Qiao, Qiquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A simple dry phys. grinding and solvent mixing approach was used to prep. tin selenide - multiwalled carbon nanotube (MWCNT) hybrid as an anode material for high performance lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  The pure tin selenide and their composites with carbon black or graphene oxides were previously reported, however no other groups have reported tin selenide/MWCNT composite as anode materials for LIBs.  The new hybrid had superior electrochem. cycling performance with higher reversible (lithiation) capacity of 882 to 651 mA hg-1 over 50 cycles compared to pure tin selenide (602 to 58 mAhg-1) or pure MWCNT (339 to 171 mAhg-1) electrodes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Alloying with Se was recently found to be an effective way to improve the cycling performance because the reduced-Se formations can act as a buffer matrix against the vol. change of electrode for IVA materials or anchors S in Li-S batteries during cycling.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Assembly of SnSe Nanoparticles Confined in Graphene for Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Xu; Zhang, Rongyu; Chen, Nan; Meng, Xing; Yang, Peilei; Wang, Chunzhong; Zhang, Yaoqing; Wei, Yingjin; Chen, Gang; Du, Fei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted much interest as a low-cost and environmentally benign energy storage system, but more attention is justifiably required to address the major tech. issues relating to the anode materials to deliver high reversible capacity, superior rate capability, and stable cyclability.  A SnSe/reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanocomposite has been prepd. by a facile ball-milling method, and its structural, morphol., and electrochem. properties have been characterized and compared with those of the bare SnSe material.  Although the redox behavior of SnSe remains nearly unchanged upon the incorporation of RGO, its electrochem. performance is significantly enhanced, as reflected by a high specific capacity of 590 mA h g-1 at 0.050 A g-1, a rate capability of 260 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1, and long-term stability over 120 cycles.  This improvement may be attributed to the high electronic cond. of RGO, which also serves as a matrix to buffer changes in vol. and maintain the mech. integrity of the electrode during (de)sodiation processes.  In view of its excellent Na+ storage performance, this SnSe/RGO nanocomposite has potential as an anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqJrnBzHpzwDLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liLWoJbDuuVbA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXitVCltLrN&amp;md5=0586979b51bf6cef096d7b4f60bb4962</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1038/nnano.2014.6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Z.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A pomegranate-inspired nanoscale design for large-volume-change lithium battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Nian; Lu, Zhenda; Zhao, Jie; McDowell, Matthew T.; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Zhao, Wenting; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">187-192</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NNAABX</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Silicon is an attractive material for anodes in energy storage devices, because it has ten times the theor. capacity of its state-of-the-art carbonaceous counterpart.  Silicon anodes can be used both in traditional lithium-ion batteries and in more recent Li-O2 and Li-S batteries as a replacement for the dendrite-forming lithium metal anodes.  The main challenges assocd. with silicon anodes are structural degrdn. and instability of the solid-electrolyte interphase caused by the large vol. change (∼300%) during cycling, the occurrence of side reactions with the electrolyte, and the low volumetric capacity when the material size is reduced to a nanometer scale.  Here, we propose a hierarchical structured silicon anode that tackles all three of these problems.  Our design is inspired by the structure of a pomegranate, where single silicon nanoparticles are encapsulated by a conductive carbon layer that leaves enough room for expansion and contraction following lithiation and delithiation.  An ensemble of these hybrid nanoparticles is then encapsulated by a thicker carbon layer in micrometre-size pouches to act as an electrolyte barrier.  As a result of this hierarchical arrangement, the solid-electrolyte interphase remains stable and spatially confined, resulting in superior cyclability (97% capacity retention after 1,000 cycles).  In addn., the microstructures lower the electrode-electrolyte contact area, resulting in high Coulombic efficiency (99.87%) and volumetric capacity (1,270 mAh cm-3), and the cycling remains stable even when the areal capacity is increased to the level of com. lithium-ion batteries (3.7 mAh cm-2).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrDypwI__SZwLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liLWoJbDuuVbA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXisFOnsL0%253D&amp;md5=bdea36fbc75cb06460488082beaea1e7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/S1006-7191(06)62081-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, L.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Transformation and slip behavior of Ni2FeGa</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sehitoglu, H.; Wang, J.; Maier, H. J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Plasticity</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">39</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">61-74</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">IJPLER</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ni2FeGa is a relatively new shape memory alloy (SMA) and exhibits superior characteristics compared to other SMAs.  Its favorable properties include low transformation stress, high reversible strains and small hysteresis.  The first stage of stress-induced martensitic transformation is from a cubic to a modulated monoclinic phase.  The energy barriers assocd. with the transformation from L21 (cubic) to modulated martensite (10M-martensite) incorporating shear and shuffle are established via atomistic simulations.  In addn., the slip resistance in the [111] direction and the dissocn. of full dislocations into partials as well as slip in the [001] direction are studied.  The unstable stacking fault energy barriers for slip by far exceeded the transformation transition state barrier permitting transformation to occur with little irreversibility.  Expts. at the meso-scale on single crystals and transmission electron microscopy were conducted to provide further proof of the pseudoelastic (reversible) behavior and the presence of anti-phase boundaries.  The results have implications for design of new shape memory alloys that possess low energy barriers for transformation coupled with high barriers for dislocation slip.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrNaaLZlBioybVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFBRvXoAGpaA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFGit7zL&amp;md5=f865569162ce579168fe7df2b1728858</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1039/c2cp42767b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Farra, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wrabetz, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schuster, M.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding CeO2 as a Deacon catalyst by probe molecule adsorption and in situ infrared characterisations</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Farra, Ramzi; Wrabetz, Sabine; Schuster, Manfred E.; Stotz, Eugen; Hamilton, Neil G.; Amrute, Amol P.; Perez-Ramirez, Javier; Lopez, Nuria; Teschner, Detre</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">CeO2 has been identified as an efficient catalyst for HCl oxidn. in the temp. range of 623-723 K provided that the oxygen content in the feed mixt. was sufficiently high to avoid bulk chlorination and thus deactivation.  Here we characterize ceria in its fresh and post-reaction states by adsorption of CO2, NH3 and CO.  Micro-calorimetry, FTIR and TPD expts. are complemented by DFT calcns., which assess adsorption energies and vibrational frequencies.  The calcns. were performed on the lowest energy surface, CeO2(111), with perfect termination and with various degrees of hydroxylation and/or chlorination.  Both expts. and calcns. suggest that the basic character of the ceria surface has been eliminated upon reaction in HCl oxidn., indicating that most of the basic lattice O sites are exchanged by chlorine and that the OH groups formed are rather acidic.  The d. and the strength of surface acidic functions increased significantly upon reaction.  An in situ FTIR reaction cell has been designed and constructed to study the evolution of OH group d. of the ceria surface during HCl oxidn.  The effect of exptl. variables, such as pO2, pHCl and temp., has been investigated.  We found that the OH group d. pos. correlated with the reactivity in the pO2 and temp. series, whereas neg. correlation was obsd. when pHCl was varied.  Implications of the above observations to the reaction mechanism are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNYbGvHFuQurVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFBRvXoAGpaA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXisValt7k%253D&amp;md5=87cb708c9656e93ca0e46df740510af6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/ic1025087"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Breathing and Twisting: An Investigation of Framework Deformation and Guest Packing in Single Crystals of a Microporous Vanadium Benzenedicarboxylate</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xiqu; Eckert, Juergen; Liu, Lumei; Jacobson, Allan J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The structural details of the compds. V benzenedicarboxylate VO(bdc)·Guest, where the Guests are the absorbed six-ring mols.: benzene, 1,4-cyclohexadiene, 1,3-cyclohexadiene, cyclohexene and cyclohexane, were detd. from single crystal x-ray data.  Crystallog. data are given.  All of the six-ring guest mols. show a high degree of ordering inside the channels of VO(bdc).  The interactions between the guests and the host framework are dominated by van der Waals bonding.  The six-ring mols. are all packed in two columns in the channels, either in herringbone or close to parallel patterns.  The packing changes the space group symmetry of VO(bdc) from Pnma to the noncentrosym. space group P212121.  The VO(bdc) framework deforms to closely adapt to the shape and thickness changes of the double columns of the guest mols.  In addn. to the well studied breathing deformation, a twisting deformation mechanism that involves a cooperative rotation of the octahedral chains accompanied by bending of the bdc ligand is apparent in the detailed structural data.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An equilibrium ab initio atomistic thermodynamics study of chlorine adsorption on the Cu(001) surface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Suleiman, Ibrahim A.; Radny, Marian W.; Gladys, Michael J.; Smith, Phillip V.; Mackie, John C.; Kennedy, Eric M.; Dlugogorski, Bogdan Z.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>

                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effects of organic cations on the defect physics of tin halide perovskites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Tingting; Zhang, Hai-Shan; Meng, Weiwei; Teng, Qiang; Liu, Meiyue; Yang, Xiaobao; Yan, Yanfa; Yip, Hin-Lap; Zhao, Yu-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin (Sn) halide perovskite absorbers have attracted much interest because of their nontoxicity as compared to their lead (Pb) halide perovskite counterparts.  Recent progress shows that the power conversion efficiency of FASnI3 (FA = HC(NH2)2) solar cells prevails over that of MASnI3 (MA = CH3NH3).  In this paper, it is shown that the org. cations, i.e., FA and MA, play a vital role in the defect properties of Sn halide perovskites.  The antibonding coupling between Sn-5s and I-5p is clearly weaker in FASnI3 than in MASnI3 due to the larger ionic size of FA, leading to higher formation energies of Sn vacancies in FASnI3.  Subsequently, the cond. of FASnI3 can be tuned from p-type to intrinsic by varying the growth conditions of the perovskite semiconductor; in contrast, MASnI3 shows unipolar high p-type cond. independent of the growth conditions.  This provides a reasonable explanation for the better performance of FASnI3-based solar cells in expts. with respect to the MASnI3-based solar cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrAjqlWffINLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrne0xZETBKw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtVCltbrN&amp;md5=51786de66033b072443b57cd0aa9c27b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.61.14095"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ferrari, A.

                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interpretation of Raman spectra of disordered and amorphous carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ferrari, A.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The model and theor. understanding of the Raman spectra in disordered and amorphous C are given.  The nature of the G and D vibration modes in graphite is analyzed in terms of the resonant excitation of π states and the long-range polarizability of π bonding.  Visible Raman data on disordered, amorphous, and diamondlike C are classified in a 3-stage model to show the factors that control the position, intensity, and widths of the G and D peaks.  The visible Raman spectra depend formally on the configuration of the sp2 sites in sp2-bonded clusters.  In cases where the sp2 clustering is controlled by the sp3 fraction, such as in as-deposited tetrahedral amorphous C (ta-C) or hydrogenated amorphous C (a-C:H) films, the visible Raman parameters can be used to derive the sp3 fraction.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqqdAvFvqG2KrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrne0xZETBKw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3cXjs1Smu7c%253D&amp;md5=e451e6f21e1f6cf375931e6a23e836bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.8b00303"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyridinic-N-Dominated Doped Defective Graphene as a Superior Oxygen Electrocatalyst for Ultrahigh-Energy-Density Zn-Air Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qichen; Ji, Yujin; Lei, Yongpeng; Wang, Yaobing; Wang, Yingde; Li, Youyong; Wang, Shuangyin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Identification of catalytic sites for O redn. reaction (ORR) and O evolution reaction (OER) in C materials remains a great challenge.  Here, we construct a pyridinic-N-dominated doped graphene with abundant vacancy defects.  The optimized sample with an ultrahigh pore vol. (3.43 cm3/g) exhibits unprecedented ORR activity with a half-wave potential of 0.85 V in alk.  For the 1st time, d. functional theory results indicate that the quadri-pyridinic N-doped C site synergized with a vacancy defect is the active site, which presents the lowest overpotential of 0.28 V for ORR and 0.28 V for OER.  The primary Zn-air batteries display a max. power d. of 115.2 mW/cm2 and an energy d. as high as 872.3 Wh/Kg.  The rechargeable Zn-air batteries illustrate a low discharge-charge overpotential and high stability (&gt;78 h).  This work provides new insight into the correlation between the N configuration synergized with a vacancy defect in electrocatalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpvdi-9D6HOprVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrne0xZETBKw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXntVKnsrs%253D&amp;md5=fd939728c92bde9e35334be17bf867d0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/S0378-7753(98)00114-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lithium insertion in ball-milled graphite</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, C. S.; Wu, G. T.; Li, W. Z.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Science S.A.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The effects of mech. milling on the microstructure, morphol. and electrochem. performance of graphite powders with respect to lithium insertion are studied.  After 150 h of ball-milling, the well-graphitized graphite has been pulverized into small particles with a size of about 50 nm, in which there are a lot of excess vacancies, microcavities and metastable carbon interstitial phases with sizes around 13 A.  Due to the large surface energy, the merging of single particles is favored and results in the formation of agglomerates with av. size about 1 μm.  Voids are formed among the agglomerated particles.  The ball-milled graphite shows reversible specific capacity for lithium of 700 mA h g-1 (L1.88C6) with large hysteresis.  The large reversible capacity is due mainly to Li doping at vacancies, microcavities (or at the edges of the metastable carbon interstitial phase) and voids.  The bonding change between the interstitial carbon and the carbon in the arom. plane that is induced by insertion of Li atoms leads to hysteresis.  During charge-discharge cycles, the reversible capacity above 1 V decreases rapidly, which may be due to some vacancies and microcavities being annihilated by moveable and some bound interstitial carbon and to electrolyte penetrating gradually into voids formed by agglomerated particles during the Li insertion and desertion process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpSI-V2zWLiHLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljrne0xZETBKw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK1cXntVGgu7Y%253D&amp;md5=8a4b99d338a17feda7c65133e0a7735f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1002/jrs.2321"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Raman spectroscopy in graphene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Malard, L. M.; Pimenta, M. A.; Dresselhaus, G.; Dresselhaus, M. S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physics Reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">473</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Recent Raman scattering studies in different types of graphene samples are reviewed here.  We first discuss the first-order and the double resonance Raman scattering mechanisms in graphene, which give rise to the most prominent Raman features.  The detn. of the no. of layers in few-layer graphene is discussed, giving special emphasis to the possibility of using Raman spectroscopy to distinguish a monolayer from few-layer graphene stacked in the Bernal (AB) configuration.  Different types of graphene samples produced both by exfoliation and using epitaxial methods are described and their Raman spectra are compared with those of 3D cryst. graphite and turbostratic graphite, in which the layers are stacked with rotational disorder.  We show that Resonance Raman studies, where the energy of the excitation laser line can be tuned continuously, can be used to probe electrons and phonons near the Dirac point of graphene and, in particular allowing a detn. to be made of the tight-binding parameters for bilayer graphene.  The special process of electron-phonon interaction that renormalizes the phonon energy giving rise to the Kohn anomaly is discussed, and is illustrated by gated expts. where the position of the Fermi level can be changed exptl.  Finally, we discuss the ability of distinguishing armchair and zig-zag edges by Raman spectroscopy and studies in graphene nanoribbons in which the Raman signal is enhanced due to resonance with singularities in the d. of electronic states.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGryevRhTj8hkLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhckPCdWtHdYg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1MXkvVSlt7o%253D&amp;md5=12bf1e7387b80149aa99cd1a9c14a6d2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2017.09.056"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Anisotropic materials are of considerable interest because of their unique combination of polarization- or direction-dependent elec., optical, and thermoelec. properties.  Low-symmetry two-dimensional (2D) materials formed by van der Waals stacking of covalently bonded at. layers are inherently anisotropic.  Layered SnSe exhibits a low degree of lattice symmetry, with a distorted NaCl structure and an in-plane anisotropy.  Here we report a systematic study of the in-plane anisotropic properties in layered SnSe, using angle-resolved Raman scattering, optical absorption, and elec. transport studies.  The optical and elec. characterization was direction-dependent, and successfully identified the cryst. orientation in the layered SnSe.  Furthermore, the dependence of Raman-intensity anisotropy on the SnSe flake thickness and the excitation wavelength were investigated by both expts. and theor. calcns.  Finally, the elec. transport studies demonstrated that few-layer SnSe field-effect transistors (FETs) have a large anisotropic ratio of carrier mobility (∼5.8) between the armchair and zigzag directions, which is a record high value reported for 2D anisotropic materials. Raman spectroscopy and XPS measurements demonstrate that higher synthesis temp. results in a higher graphitization degree of the polymer skeleton and fewer Se-Se bonds.  The Se/PAN electrodes present excellent rate capability and extra-long cycle life due to their fast electrochem. reaction kinetics and high structural stability.  A reversible specific capacity of ∼325 mA h g-1 for the Se/PAN composite synthesized at 500° was obtained with a capacity decay of only 2.6% (based on the 2nd cycle) after 1500 cycles.  Also, the correlation between their structure and electrochem. performance was elucidated.  The Se/PAN composites obtained at higher temp. show better cycling stability but lower capacity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoy-q1j68xG2rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYf1S7BTP4dg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjtFKmsbc%253D&amp;md5=fb652ada84e7b577be6885b30abf0e11</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201704079"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sha, L.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Self-Repairing Cathode Material for Lithium-Selenium Batteries: Se-C Chemically Bonded Selenium-Graphene Composite</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sha, Linna; Gao, Peng; Ren, Xiaochen; Chi, Qianqian; Chen, Yujin; Yang, Piaoping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">24</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2151-2156</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-Se batteries, using Se as a cathode material, exhibit some notable advantages, such as high discharge rates and good cycling performance, due to their high elec. cond., high output voltages, and high volumetric capacity d.  However, an important problem, termed the shuttle effect, can lead to capacity decay in Li-Se cells (and in Li-S cells), which arises from aggregation and the loss of Se or S from the cathode into the electrolyte.  Here, in order to solve this problem, a new self-repairing system was devised, in which some Se atoms are chem. bonded to the C atoms of graphene and act as reclaiming points for dissocd. Se atoms through the establishment of -Se-Se-Se- chains.  Se-decorated graphene (Se-GE) was 1st constructed through a facile high-energy ball-milling process.  Its formation was confirmed by XRD, SEM, HRTEM, XPS, and Raman analyses.  As we anticipated, in examg. cell properties, the as-prepd. Se-GE composite underwent an initial capacity decay in the 1st 20 cycles (1050-750 mAh/g, ∼29% loss), but the capacity then reverted to 970 mAh/g (∼92% of the initial value).  Other measurements were also consistent with the recapture of dissocd. Se atoms.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqgQaP3cppOibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYf1S7BTP4dg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXovFGlsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=ef4efb04cee8761be4d8848af49f0de3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2014.07.012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, L.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Confined selenium within porous carbon nanospheres as cathode for advanced Li-Se batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhen; Yuan, Lixia; Yi, Ziqi; Liu, Yang; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Selenium (Se) is potential as a promising alternative cathode material for high-energy batteries because of its comparable theor. volumetric capacity d. (3240 mAh cm-3) to sulfur (3467 mAh cm-3) and a much higher electronic cond. (1×10-3 S m-1) than sulfur (5×10-28 S m-1).  In this work, we developed a novel Se composite confined within porous carbon nanospheres (Se/PCNs) as cathode for advanced Li-Se battery.  A Se loading as high as 70.5 wt% is attained in such composite.  The Se/PCNs cathode shows high volumetric capacity d. of 3150 mAh/cm3 and excellent rate capability (retains 57% of the theor. capacity at 20 C).  Remarkably, it exhibits impressive cycling stability over 1200 cycles with a capacity decay as low as ∼0.03% per cycle.  The superior overall battery performance can be ascribed to high loading of active material, effective protective film formed on the surface of the active material, and strong adsorbing ability of Se/Li2Sex provided by the micropore-rich carbon structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqk3eWM2nsCobVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhYf1S7BTP4dg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlCitLrM&amp;md5=7d4d24f91936a1d6e16d1a4392506aec</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1039/C7NR05556K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Y.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controlling the Sn-C bonds content in SnO2@CNTs composite to form in situ pulverized structure for enhanced electrochemical kinetics</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Yayi; Huang, Jianfeng; Qi, Hui; Cao, Liyun; Luo, Xiaomin; Li, Jiayin; Xu, Zhanwei; Yang, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Sn-C bonding content between the SnO2 and CNTs interface was controlled by the hydrothermal method and subsequent heat treatment.  Electrochem. anal. found that the SnO2@CNTs with high Sn-C bonding content exhibited much higher capacity contribution from alloying and conversion reaction compared with the low content of Sn-C bonding even after 200 cycles.  The high Sn-C bonding content enabled the SnO2 nanoparticles to stabilize on the CNTs surface, realizing an in situ pulverization process of SnO2.  The in situ pulverized structure was beneficial to maintain the close electrochem. contact of the working electrode during the long-term cycling and provide ultrafast transfer paths for lithium ions and electrons, which promoted the alloying and conversion reaction kinetics greatly.  Therefore, the SnO2@CNTs composite with high Sn-C bonding content displayed highly reversible alloying and conversion reaction.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sn-C bonding riveted SnSe nanoplates vertically grown on nitrogen-doped carbon nanobelts for high-performance sodium-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ren, Xiaochuan; Wang, Jinsong; Zhu, Daming; Li, Qingwei; Tian, Weifeng; Wang, Lei; Zhang, Jiabao; Miao, Ling; Chu, Paul K.; Huo, Kaifu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnSe is a promising anode material in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity (780 mA h g-1) and natural abundance.  Herein, we report SnSe nanoplates vertically grown on nitrogen-doped carbon (SnSe/NC) with strong Sn-C bonding for high-performance anode in SIBs, which are synthesized by a facial cation-exchange strategy.  The vertically grown SnSe nanoplates with large interplanar spacing (0.58 nm), strong electronic coupling of Sn-C bonding between SnSe and NC facilitate the fast electron/ion transfer, enabling high pseudocapacitive Na-ion storage and enhanced power capability.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Simple, yet predictive bonding models are essential achievements of chem.  In the solid state, in particular, they often appear in the form of visual bonding indicators.  Because the latter require the crystal orbitals to be constructed from local basis sets, the application of the most popular d.-functional theory codes (namely, those based on plane waves and pseudopotentials) appears as being ill-fitted to retrieve the chem. bonding information.  In this paper, we describe a way to re-ext. Hamilton-weighted populations from plane-wave electronic-structure calcns. to develop a tool analogous to the familiar crystal orbital Hamilton population (COHP) method.  We derive the new technique, dubbed "projected COHP" (pCOHP), and demonstrate its viability using examples of covalent, ionic, and metallic crystals (diamond, GaAs, CsCl, and Na).  For the first time, this chem. bonding information is directly extd. from the results of plane-wave calcns.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqJK3R7pxAxX7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljO58gab7cIGg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXlslKitr8%253D&amp;md5=4b8024fd1ed30e78710deaaf6d0d3796</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.76.214432"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bellini, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Di Giustino, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Manghi, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ab Initio Study of The Fe/NiO Interface: Structural and Magnetic Properties</span>. <i>Phys. A decrease of the oxidn. peaks at 1.3 and 1.9 V in CV curves of Li/SnSe batteries was obsd., indicating the reversible formation and decompn. of reactions of Li2Se. The as-painted SnSe nanocrystals/carbon fabric electrodes exhibit an outstanding capacity of 676 mA-h/g after 80 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA/g and a considerable high-rate capability in lithium storage because of the excellent ion transport from the electrolyte to the active materials and the efficient charge transport between current collector and electrode materials.                         cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">518-522</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7ifz8L3ww4g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref60'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1038/nmat2612"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brezesinski, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tolbert, S.                         cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ordered mesoporous α-MoO3 with iso-oriented nanocrystalline walls for thin-film pseudocapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Brezesinski, Torsten; Wang, John; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Capacitive energy storage is distinguished from other types of electrochem. energy storage by short charging times and the ability to deliver significantly more power than batteries.  A limitation to this technol. is its low energy d. and there is interest in exploring pseudo-capacitive materials where faradaic mechanisms offer increased energy storage.  The capacitive charge-storage properties of mesoporous films of iso-oriented α-MoO3 are superior to those of either mesoporous amorphous material or nonporous cryst. MoO3.  Whereas both cryst. and amorphous mesoporous materials show redox pseudo-capacitance, the iso-oriented layered cryst. domains enable Li ions to be inserted into the van der Waals gaps of the α-MoO3.  Probably this extra contribution arises from an intercalation pseudo-capacitance, which occurs on the same timescale as redox pseudo-capacitance.  The result is increased charge-storage capacity without compromising charge/discharge kinetics in mesoporous cryst. MoO3.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp77bOsasmjcrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7ifz8L3ww4g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXhtVOnt78%253D&amp;md5=b6e743b60b27d6e0dfcabcf281d3d475</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref61'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA03083A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.                         cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoporous Mo2C/N-doped carbon heteronanowires as high-rate and long-life anode materials for Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Lichun; Li, Xiang; He, Sina; Du, Gaohui; Yu, Xiang; Liu, Jiangwen; Gao, Qingsheng; Hu, Renzong; Zhu, Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
